[source:Type_of_Cancer, Stage_of_Cancer, Distant Metastasis]\nThe purpose of this visit was to start your care, finish checking where the cancer has spread, and plan for treatment to help you feel better and live longer. [source:Type_of_Cancer]\nYour cancer has spread to multiple areas including your lungs, liver, the lining of your abdomen, and your ovaries. [source:Metastasis]\nA scan showed a new mass in your armpit area near your old surgery site, which looks like the cancer has come back locally. [source:findings]\nYour physical exam confirmed a lump in your armpit and an enlarged liver with masses in your belly. [source:findings]\nWe also noted that your appendix might have a fluid-filled cyst, but it does not look like an infection. [source:goals_of_treatment]\n\n**What is the plan going forward?**\nYou will have a biopsy of the mass in your armpit to confirm the type of cancer cells. [source:imaging_plan]\nYou will have blood tests including a complete blood count, liver tests, and specific cancer markers. "Dear Patient, [source:none]\nWe hope you are doing well. We are writing this letter to help you understand what happened during your recent visit. [source:none]\n\n**Why did you come to the clinic?**\nYou came in for a new consultation to discuss your treatment plan after surgery for breast cancer. [source:summary]\nYou are a 29-year-old patient with a history of invasive ductal carcinoma, which is cancer that started in the milk ducts. [source:Type_of_Cancer]\nYour cancer was originally stage II-III and involved the left breast and lymph nodes under the arm. [source:Stage_of_Cancer]\nYou had surgery to remove the tumor and check the lymph nodes under the arm, known as a lumpectomy and ALND. [source:summary]\nYou also had treatment before surgery to shrink the cancer, known as neoadjuvant therapy, but it was not completed. [source:summary]\nWe are here to plan the next steps to prevent the cancer from coming back, known as adjuvant therapy. [source:goals_of_treatment]\n\n**What's new or changed since your last visit?**\nAfter your surgery, no cancer was found in the breast tissue itself, which is a good sign. [source:findings]\nHowever, cancer was still found in some of the lymph nodes under the arm. [source:response_assessment]\nSpecifically, cancer was found in 3 of the 28 lymph nodes that were removed. [source:findings]\nThe cancer cells had grown outside the lymph node capsule, which is called extranodal extension. [source:findings]\nThere was also inflammation in the lymph nodes called necrotizing lymphadenitis. [source:findings]\nRecent scans showed no signs that the cancer has spread to other parts of your body. [source:findings]\nYour physical exam showed you are feeling well with no pain or lumps. [source:findings]\n\n**What treatment or medication changes were made?**\nYou are recommended to start a new chemotherapy treatment called AC, which includes doxorubicin and cyclophosphamide. [source:medication_plan]\nThis treatment will be given for 4 cycles. [source:therapy_plan]\nAfter finishing AC, you will start another treatment called T-DM1 for one year. [source:medication_plan]\nYou also have pain medications available, including acetaminophen, ibuprofen, and oxyCODONE, if needed. [source:supportive_meds]\n\n**What is the plan going forward?**\nYou are referred to have a port placed to make it easier to receive your treatments. [source:procedure_plan]\nYou will need an echocardiogram, which is an ultrasound of your heart, before starting the new chemotherapy. [source:imaging_plan]\nRadiation therapy is recommended after you finish the AC chemotherapy. [source:radiotherapy_plan]\nWe plan to speak with you again this coming week to discuss the treatment plan and support. [source:follow up]\nNo genetic testing or referrals to other specialists are planned at this time. [source:Genetics,Specialty]\nAdvance care planning was not discussed during this visit. [source:Advance care]\n\nThank you for trusting us with your care. [source:none]\nPlease feel free to contact us if you have any questions. [source:none]\nSincerely, Your Care Team [source:none]"

"Dear Patient, [source:none]\nWe hope you are doing well. [source:none]\nWe are writing this letter to help you understand what happened during your recent visit. [source:none]\n\n**Why did you come to the clinic?**\nYou came in for a consultation to discuss further treatment for your breast cancer after surgery. [source:summary]\nYou have invasive ductal carcinoma, which is cancer that started in the milk ducts. [source:Type_of_Cancer]\nYour cancer is Stage IA, meaning it is small and has not spread to other parts of your body. [source:Stage_of_Cancer]\nThe cancer cells have receptors for estrogen and progesterone but do not have a protein called HER2. [source:Type_of_Cancer]\nThe goal of your treatment is to cure the cancer. [source:goals_of_treatment]\n\n**What's new or changed since your last visit?**\nYour surgery to remove the tumor (lumpectomy) was successful. [source:findings]\nThe removed tissue showed no cancer at the edges and no cancer in the lymph nodes under your arm. [source:findings]\nYou are currently feeling well, with only some minor numbness from the surgery. [source:findings]\nYou have not started any new treatment yet, so there is no change in the cancer to report. [source:response_assessment]\n\n**What treatment or medication changes were made?**\nYou are recommended to start hormonal therapy to help prevent the cancer from coming back. [source:medication_plan]\nThis treatment will last for at least five years. [source:therapy_plan]\nYou will take either tamoxifen or a type of medication called an aromatase inhibitor. [source:medication_plan]\nThe choice between these two options depends on whether you are menopausal, which will be checked with blood tests. [source:therapy_plan]\nYou will also need radiation therapy to the breast to complete your treatment. [source:radiotherapy_plan]\n\n**What is the plan going forward?**\nYou will have blood tests to check your hormone levels. [source:lab_plan]\nYou will have a baseline bone density scan (DXA scan) to check your bone health. [source:imaging_plan]\nYou are referred to a genetics specialist to check for inherited cancer risks based on your family history. [source:Genetic_Testing_Plan]\nYou are referred to a nutritionist to discuss your diet. [source:Nutrition]\nYou have a specialist consultation scheduled for tomorrow to discuss your radiation therapy. [source:Specialty]\nIf genetic testing shows a high risk, you might choose to have your other breast removed, which would delay the radiation therapy. [source:radiotherapy_plan]\nYou will have a follow-up visit after the radiation therapy to start your hormonal medication. [source:follow up]\nYour care team will not discuss advance care planning at this time. [source:Advance care]\n\nThank you for trusting us with your care. [source:none]\nPlease feel free to contact us if you have any questions. [source:none]\nSincerely, Your Care Team [source:none]"

"Dear Patient, [source:none]\nWe hope you are doing well. [source:none]\nWe are writing this letter to help you understand what happened during your recent visit. [source:none]\n\n**Why did you come to the clinic?**\nYou came in for a new visit to discuss your breast cancer diagnosis and treatment options. [source:summary]\nYou have a type of breast cancer called invasive ductal carcinoma, which started in the milk ducts. [source:Type_of_Cancer]\nThe cancer is at Stage IA, which means it is small and has not spread to other parts of your body. [source:Stage_of_Cancer, Distant Metastasis]\nYou also have a related condition called encapsulated papillary carcinoma, which is similar to a non-invasive form of breast cancer. [source:findings]\n\n**What's new or changed since your last visit?**\nA surgery called a lumpectomy was done to remove the tumor from your left breast. [source:findings]\nThe surgery removed an 8 millimeter tumor that is Grade 1, which means the cells look fairly normal. [source:findings]\nThe edges of the removed tissue were checked, and the cancer was not found at the edges, which is good. [source:findings]\nA small number of cancer cells were found in one of the three lymph nodes checked under your arm. [source:findings]\nTests showed that the cancer cells have receptors for estrogen and progesterone, but not the HER2 protein. [source:findings]\nYour breast exam shows that the area where surgery was done is healing well. Serum creatinine level is affected by multiple factors besides GFR, including creatinine generation (which is correlated primarily with muscle mass) and renal tubular secretion of creatinine (which can be affected by certain medications). We also discussed the importance of exercise in helping to alleviate this symptoms.     We reviewed data from ***** trial which evaluated 5,015 patients with stage II/III breast cancer, March 30 involved nodes, and a RS ? 25. Patients were assigned to receive either endocrine therapy or endocrine therapy plus standard chemotherapy. [source:none]\n\n**Why did you come to the clinic?**\nYou came in for a new consultation to discuss treatment options for your breast cancer and to talk about preserving your ability to have children in the future. [source:summary]\nYou have a type of breast cancer called invasive ductal carcinoma that is hormone receptor positive but does not have the HER2 protein. [source:Type_of_Cancer]\nThe cancer was found in your left breast and is currently considered Stage IIA. [source:Stage_of_Cancer]\nThe cancer has not spread to other parts of your body. [source:Metastasis]\n\n**What's new or changed since your last visit?**\nYou had surgery to remove the tumor from your left breast, and the results showed a small amount of cancer in one of the lymph nodes under your arm. [source:findings]\nYour cancer cells have high levels of hormone receptors, which means they grow in response to hormones. [source:findings]\nA urine test was done to check for pregnancy, and the result was negative. [source:lab_summary]\nYou are currently not on any treatment, so there is no change in the cancer to report yet. [source:response_assessment]\n\n**What treatment or medication changes were made?**\nYou will start a treatment called hormonal therapy to help prevent the cancer from coming back. [source:goals_of_treatment]\nThis treatment will include a medication to stop your ovaries from working and another medication to block hormones, but it will start after you finish harvesting eggs for fertility preservation. [source:medication_plan]\nYou will need to take this hormonal therapy for at least five years. [source:therapy_plan]\nYou were also given a medication called ondansetron to help with nausea if needed. [source:supportive_meds]\n\n**What is the plan going forward?**\nYou are referred to a specialist in reproductive health to discuss fertility preservation options. [source:Others]\nYou will have a CT scan of your chest, abdomen, and pelvis, as well as a bone scan to check for any spread of the cancer. [source:imaging_plan]\nYou will have a genetic test done on your tumor to learn more about its biology and to see if chemotherapy might be helpful. [source:genetic_testing_plan]\nYou are scheduled to return to the clinic in three weeks. [source:follow up]\nNo advance care planning was discussed during this visit. [source:Advance care]\n\nThank you for trusting us with your care. [source:none]\nPlease feel free to contact us if you have any questions. [source:none]\nSincerely, Your Care Team [source:none]"

[source:Type_of_Cancer]\nThe cancer is at Stage I, which means it is small and has not spread to other parts of your body. [source:Stage_of_Cancer, Metastasis]\nYour cancer cells have a protein called estrogen receptor (ER) and progesterone receptor (PR) that are positive, but they do not have a protein called HER2. [source:Type_of_Cancer]\nThe goal of your treatment is to cure the cancer. [source:goals_of_treatment]\n\n**What's new or changed since your last visit?**\nA biopsy of a lump in your left breast confirmed the cancer. [source:findings]\nThe cancer cells were found to be at least 11 millimeters in size and were classified as grade 2. [source:findings]\nTests showed that the cancer cells have the estrogen and progesterone receptors but not the HER2 protein. [source:findings]\nAn MRI scan showed a small area in your left breast that looked suspicious, but a repeat biopsy of that area was negative for cancer. [source:findings]\nOther scans of your chest and abdomen showed no signs that the cancer has spread to other organs. [source:findings]\nYour physical exam showed that you are doing well with no signs of acute distress. [source:findings]\n\n**What treatment or medication changes were made?**\nYou are scheduled to have surgery to remove the tumor, which is called a lumpectomy. [source:therapy_plan]\nDuring the surgery, you will receive radiation therapy directly to the area where the tumor was removed. [source:radiotherapy_plan]\nYou will also have surgery to rebuild your breast. [source:procedure_plan]\nAfter the surgery, you will likely need treatment with chemotherapy to help prevent the cancer from coming back. [source:therapy_plan]\nYou will also need to take medication to block the effects of estrogen, which is called endocrine therapy. [source:medication_plan]\nThis medication may be Tamoxifen or a treatment to stop your ovaries from working plus another medicine. [source:medication_plan]\nBecause you will get radiation during the surgery, you will not need radiation treatment after the surgery is finished.
